    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/180614-nirkatze"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/180614-nirkatze">Nirkatze</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Also, Helen Beckitt's daughter took a bullet meant FOR Marcone. He didn't fire the shot, he was the target. By the end of White Night, it is revealed <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Also, Helen Beckitt's daughter took a bullet meant FOR Marcone. He didn't fire the shot, he was the target. By the end of White Night, it is revealed that the girl is the one Marcone stole the Shroud for in Death Masks, that she is not truly dead but in a coma. She is the deep secret shame he would do anything to undo. He hasn't told Helen, but in a way, the same thing that drives her drives him. The could have found that in each other, or Helen could just be biding her time. The true why is left open to reader interpretation.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/111252118-jerry-r"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/111252118-jerry-r">Jerry R</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Because magic empowers the herd (humanity). They specifically target female practitioners because magic usually descends via the mothers side. if they<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Because magic empowers the herd (humanity). They specifically target female practitioners because magic usually descends via the mothers side. if they can eliminate the 'mutants' as they refer to human magic users, it's easier for them to hunt.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3091105846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2362429942129599394"><b>4.5/5 stars<br/><br/>I've mentioned this several times, but it's always safe to rely on <i>The Dresden Files</i> for a quick entertaining read.</b><br/><br/>A serial killer is on the loose, and they’re targeting practitioners of magic. And to make things worse, all the evidence seems to point towards Thomas as the perpetrator. Harry Blackstone Copperfield Dresden, of course, won’t allow this to happen. That’s the premise of <i>White Night</i>, but surprisingly, there’s actually less focus on investigation now compared to the previou</span>
  <span id="freeText2362429942129599394" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 stars<br><br>I've mentioned this several times, but it's always safe to rely on <i>The Dresden Files</i> for a quick entertaining read.</b><br><br>A serial killer is on the loose, and they’re targeting practitioners of magic. And to make things worse, all the evidence seems to point towards Thomas as the perpetrator. Harry Blackstone Copperfield Dresden, of course, won’t allow this to happen. That’s the premise of <i>White Night</i>, but surprisingly, there’s actually less focus on investigation now compared to the previous books in the series. I personally consider this a good direction for the series; I’ve always preferred reading about the magic or world-building aspect of the series more than the investigation parts anyway. I found <i>White Night</i> to be as good as <i>Dead Beat</i> in overall quality due to few reasons.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“People love dogs. You can never go wrong adding a dog to the story.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>That’s not what I’m going to talk about, but that’s not wrong. Yes, Mouse is here, and he’s still the goodest boy. If you’ve read and enjoyed the series up to this ninth installment, then you should know already that the series is filled with tons of endearing cast of characters with well-put characterizations and developments, but they take turns in each volume. Sometimes a character appears, sometimes they don’t. In <i>White Night</i>, most of the relationship development occurs between Harry, Molly, and Ramirez—another character I didn’t expect I would find myself invested in this much. As I repeatedly said throughout my reviews, the surprisingly delightful characterizations for Harry, the side characters, and their development with each other is one of the biggest selling points of the series for me, and that remains true in this book. I also utterly loved the discussion and passages about power, loneliness, and pain.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Everyone is down on pain, because they forget something important about it: Pain is for the living. Only the dead don't feel it.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Then there’s also this line, which probably would—sadly—continue to be evident until the world explodes:<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Bigots see something they expect and then they stop thinking about what is in front of them. It's probably how they got to be bigots in the first place.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Isn’t it so true?<br><br>Speaking of being pleasantly surprised earlier, I actually liked reading the action sequences here. It never felt boring, and wow, the battle against the ghouls did get crazy. For me, the pacing and longevity of the action sequences in the series have always been a persisting issue; <i>Dead Beat</i> was the only time I can say I thoroughly enjoyed reading every action and battle scenes within a volume of the series. It feels good that I can finally add another installment to that small list. The actions in the last few chapters of this novel were gripping, and I definitely hope this level of quality in the actions will be maintained or maybe even surpassed in the sequels.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Knowledge is the ultimate weapon. It always has been.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>White Night</i> has the most satisfying ending in the series so far. Not only the case file felt properly concluded, but the ending also made me smile. (I mean, c’mon, there’s even a Tiger Balm! That’s something I use that I thought would never appear in an urban fantasy novel!) Suffice to say that overall, same as <i>Dead Beat</i>, <i>White Night</i> is one of my favorite installment in the series so far. I’m sure this position won’t last long; at the rapid rate the series is ascending in enjoyment, I’m confident the next book will be as good or maybe even better. I’ll start reading <i>Small Favor</i> two weeks from now.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Passion has overthrown tyrants and freed prisoners and slaves. Passion has brought justice where there was savagery. Passion has created freedom where there was nothing but fear. Passion has helped souls rise from the ashes of their horrible lives and build something better, stronger, more beautiful.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Picture: <i>White Night</i> by Vincent Chong</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1593941978i/29764941._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780356500355/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><b>You can find <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2020/07/05/book-review-white-night-the-dresden-files-9-by-jim-butcher/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u> and the rest of my reviews at <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b><br><br><i>Special thanks to my Patrons on <b><u><a href="https://www.patreon.com/petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Patreon</a></u></b> for giving me extra support towards my passion for reading and reviewing!<br><br>My Patrons: Alfred, Devin, Hamad, Jimmy Nutts, Joie, Mike, Miracle, Nicholas.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2362429942129599394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2388231374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9596354396298351980"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>So darn good. <i>White Night</i> was such an engrossing and entertaining read that I finished it in under 1.5 days. The combination of an intriguing plot and close to perfect pacing was a real page-turner. And the action sequence during the climax of this book was pretty insane. <br/><br/>But the highlight for me was the character development - be it for Harry, or the main supporting cast of Thomas, Murphy and Mouse (yea, he's a dog but that's all the more reason why I love him so much). I'm so investe</span>
  <span id="freeText9596354396298351980" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br />So darn good. <i>White Night</i> was such an engrossing and entertaining read that I finished it in under 1.5 days. The combination of an intriguing plot and close to perfect pacing was a real page-turner. And the action sequence during the climax of this book was pretty insane. <br /><br />But the highlight for me was the character development - be it for Harry, or the main supporting cast of Thomas, Murphy and Mouse (yea, he's a dog but that's all the more reason why I love him so much). I'm so invested in all of them now that I fear for their safety. Not so much for Harry yet because I do know that there are many more books to go, but who knows whether the rest would be safe from serious harm. Harry's characterisation kept on improving with each subsequent book, and the emotional resonance which was missing for me in the earlier books is now well and truly established. <br /><br />It is also a well-established opinion among readers of <i>The Dresden Files</i> that the series continues to improve from here and I'm so excited to keep reading. If this keeps up, I foresee the first 5-star rating coming up soon.</span>

<div id="review_168644201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168644201" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168644201?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-urban-fantasy">genre-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=z-audiobooks">z-audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168644201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11547931889303167439">Classic Dresden files book, so it was good. But this read just like about three or four of his other books...<br/><br/>**Set in Chicago...<u>again</u><br/>**White Court vamps are evil and the war is ongoing...still<br/>**Bob the pervy skull gets a complete intro and helps out with witty candor...<br/>**Thomas is hungry and Harry is suspicious of him<br/>**Harry STILL doesn't get laid<br/><br/><br/>I'm ready for Butcher to move on to a new subject, a new setting, and to settle the score with all of the above. How many times does Bob need an introd</span>
  <span id="freeText11547931889303167439" style="display:none">Classic Dresden files book, so it was good. But this read just like about three or four of his other books...<br /><br />**Set in Chicago...<u>again</u><br />**White Court vamps are evil and the war is ongoing...still<br />**Bob the pervy skull gets a complete intro and helps out with witty candor...<br />**Thomas is hungry and Harry is suspicious of him<br />**Harry STILL doesn't get laid<br /><br /><br />I'm ready for Butcher to move on to a new subject, a new setting, and to settle the score with all of the above. How many times does Bob need an introduction? If someone picks up book nine of a series and expects to understand everything, it's their own damn fault. I don't want to read the same thing nine times!<br /><br />Same with Harry's chivalrous nature. I'm about tired of how Harry has to repeatedly tout his own heroics. Oh, the women and children...save the women and children! Must not see them suffer, even if they are cutting off my good parts and torturing my loved ones. If it's a woman, Harry <b>will</b> tell us, multiple times in the same book, how he can't bring himself to be less than courteous.<br /><br />I think the reason this book bothered me so much was that the last book in the series had a different vibe to it, and I was so very interested the entire time I read it. That book took us to the land of fairy, gave Harry an apprentice, and I felt like it moved the series forward a few steps. So I expected this one to keep moving forward. Not so. It sort of moved backward, and it's annoying. <br /><br />I listened to the audio again...James Marsters does an amazing job. You can hear how into his role he is, and it seems as if he has become more and more Harry Dresden with each installment. <br /><br />I probably should give this more than two stars, but I ended up skimming through soooo much of it, and I really don't feel like I missed anything. I think I could have skipped the entire book and been just fine moving on to the next one. Maybe I need to just give the series a break for awhile so that it's all new again, because at this point, if the next book isn't vastly different, I may give up on Dresden.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11547931889303167439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3837965551454736863">“Better the devil you know than the devil you don't.”<br/><br/>Jim Butcher’s ninth Harry Dresden novel, first published in 2007, is about a lot of things, as all of these entertaining books are, but the central theme seems to be picking the lesser of two evils, or working a Corleone plan by keeping your friends close but your enemies closer.<br/><br/>Several of the recent Dresden novels have involved Harry’s tenuous connection to the White Court of vampires and this one finds our hero drawn once more into a confron</span>
  <span id="freeText3837965551454736863" style="display:none">“Better the devil you know than the devil you don't.”<br><br>Jim Butcher’s ninth Harry Dresden novel, first published in 2007, is about a lot of things, as all of these entertaining books are, but the central theme seems to be picking the lesser of two evils, or working a Corleone plan by keeping your friends close but your enemies closer.<br><br>Several of the recent Dresden novels have involved Harry’s tenuous connection to the White Court of vampires and this one finds our hero drawn once more into a confrontation with this lascivious group of succubae. There's also the tracking down of a magical serial killer, some neanderthal ghouls and Bob the talking skull.<br><br>Fans of the series know that the vampires are divided into three main groups, or courts, the Red, Black and White. The Red Court vampires are non-human and demonic in true form, hiding behind a magical veil. The Black court types are the “classic” vampires – undead creatures feasting on human blood and counting stuff on Sesame Street.<br><br>The White Court are the most human like and feed not on blood so much as emotion – sex, fear, despair. They also like to operate behind the scenes by manipulation, persuasion and subterfuge.<br><br>Also present is a list of Dresden recurring characters including Johnny Marcone and Ramirez.<br><br>Full of Butcher’s can of corn humor, some introspective philosophical musings, as well as more than an ample allowance of ACTION! this is another fun entry into the Dresden files.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1582479157i/29009555._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1640585882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1640585882" />
    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1640585882?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/18663180-white-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=top-priority">top-priority</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1640585882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16783526963889974569"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Magic is groovy, but when it comes to dealing out death, regular mortal know-how can be just as impressive."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This one hit all the right chords for me. I would rank it in my top 2 or 3 Dresden books so far. But, there is still a long way to go. That final battle was intense as hell. Definitely, one of the top action scenes in this series so far. <br/><br/>In this installment Harry gets pulled into a case involving a serial killer. But, not just any serial killer. This one preys on the magical c</span>
  <span id="freeText16783526963889974569" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Magic is groovy, but when it comes to dealing out death, regular mortal know-how can be just as impressive."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />This one hit all the right chords for me. I would rank it in my top 2 or 3 Dresden books so far. But, there is still a long way to go. That final battle was intense as hell. Definitely, one of the top action scenes in this series so far. <br /><br />In this installment Harry gets pulled into a case involving a serial killer. But, not just any serial killer. This one preys on the magical community, and he/she is making it look like suicides. Only someone with magical talent and just so happens to be a detective could find the clues being left behind. Enter Harry Blackstone Copperfield Dresden.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Anger is just anger. It isn't good. It isn't bad. It just is. What you do with it is what matters. It's like anything else. You can use it to build or to destroy. You just have to make the choice."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />The magical elements and Harry's detective work were well balanced in this book. Most of the time the magic tends to overwhelm the actual case. Also, Mouse is fast becoming my favorite side character in this series. I love Bob the skull, but I mean who doesn't want a dog like Mouse as your sidekick right. <br /><br />I know I have said this in one of my earlier reviews, but this series has so many moving parts. Each book is vastly different and still retains the same overall feel of the main plot. Butcher is so good as creating a magical underworld right in our own backyard that it feels almost believable. I wasn't getting tired of this series at all, but this installment really has me excited for the direction the story is going. It just feels like the intensity level is being ramped up and the stakes get higher with each volume and I am loving it.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Life's easier when you can write off others as monsters, as demons, as horrible threats that must be hated and feared. The thing is, you can't do that without becoming them, just a little."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 5 stars *****</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16783526963889974569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_22675160" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22675160" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1177534-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593697601p2/1177534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22675160?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1177534-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans who've read previous Dresden Files novels</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=series-challenge">series-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22675160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10402411525456507221">The ninth Harry Dresden novel is the series riches and most densely plotted to date--and the first in the series I can't recommend to someone coming to the series cold. <br/><br/>Not that this is a bad thing. It's a great thing for readers of the Dresden Files. While Jim Butcher does deliver payoffs and resolutions in his previous eight books, here in "White Night" he steps that up a notch, bringing back old friends and enemies to Harry Dresden's world all while building on several key plotlines from the </span>
  <span id="freeText10402411525456507221" style="display:none">The ninth Harry Dresden novel is the series riches and most densely plotted to date--and the first in the series I can't recommend to someone coming to the series cold. <br /><br />Not that this is a bad thing. It's a great thing for readers of the Dresden Files. While Jim Butcher does deliver payoffs and resolutions in his previous eight books, here in "White Night" he steps that up a notch, bringing back old friends and enemies to Harry Dresden's world all while building on several key plotlines from the last several novels as the war between the various supernatural factions begins to reach a boiling point and Harry Dresden is, once again, at the center of it all.<br /><br />If you're coming into this cold, you'll be thorougly confused. If you've read the previous eight books, you're probably going to eat this up with a spoon, eagerly turning the pages, waiting for the next development to hit. <br /><br />Murphy calls Harry in on a case that may or may not have supernatural undercurrents. Harry discovers a message that only he could find and begins to look into a series of similar deaths. Finding the same message, hidden in the same way, Harry suspects a serial killer is on the loose in the supernatural community. The problem: the number one suspect is his half-brother Thomas. <br /><br />Harry is convinced Thomas isn't the killer, but the evidence is pretty damning. Harry begins to pull at the threads and uncovers someone or something targeting women of a Wiccan order. They've already asked for help from Harry's first love, Elaine, who is now a private eye in Los Angeles who investigates the supernatural. <br /><br />All of this we find in the first hundred or so pages and that's just when it gets interesting. Butcher weaves together a complex, fascinating story with Harry firmly at the center, trying to find the pieces of the puzzle and prove the innocence of his half-brother. In the midst of al this, we learn about the politics of the current battle between the Red Court and the White Council and how Harry fits into a plan to possibly tip the balance. Along the way, we meet old enemies and have call backs to the first novel in the series. <br /><br />About the only thing I found frustrating about this novel is that in the last book, Harry determined a secret group was plotting within the power ranks of the White Council. And while this development is brought up, we never get any movement toward discovering who or what is behind this and what their agenda is. I realize that Butcher may be setting up some things for future installments, but a revelation this big seems a bit difficult to only pay lip service to in the story.<br /><br />But that's the only detraction I can find in this superb entry in the Dresden series. Butcher keeps getting better and better, continuing to keep the Dresden Files as one of the must reads on my bookshelf. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10402411525456507221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2570969298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2570969298" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2570969298?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2570969298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer582792658491765645">Someone is killing people in Chicago and leaving clues that only a person with magical ability, like a wizard named Harry Dresden, could see. Why would they do that?<br/><br/>Meanwhile, most everything else in Harry's life is going spectacularly wrong. He has an unruly apprentice who had an unfortunate brush with dark magic awhile back. The White Council is still at war with the Red Vampire Court which was Harry's fault to begin with, but we don't need to go into all that.<br/><br/>He's still got a fallen angel's s</span>
  <span id="freeText582792658491765645" style="display:none">Someone is killing people in Chicago and leaving clues that only a person with magical ability, like a wizard named Harry Dresden, could see. Why would they do that?<br /><br />Meanwhile, most everything else in Harry's life is going spectacularly wrong. He has an unruly apprentice who had an unfortunate brush with dark magic awhile back. The White Council is still at war with the Red Vampire Court which was Harry's fault to begin with, but we don't need to go into all that.<br /><br />He's still got a fallen angel's shadow in his head, trying to convince him to wield a coin that will give Harry unimaginable power but also consume his soul. Thomas, the vampire, has been acting really weird and he's probably eating people again which, vampires do, but it's kind of a problem because Harry is supposed to be protecting people.<br /><br />And now this, a serial killer. Perfect.<br /><br /><i>The Dresden Files</i>, as a series, is really starting to come together. I like how Jim Butcher starts to layer the books on top of each other, each plot line leading to more complications and depth.<br /><br /><i>Normally, Wardens existed to police wizards, to make sure that they didn't use their power against the rest of humanity in violation of the Laws of Magic. Things weren't normal."</i> pg 59, ebook.<br /><br /> Harry has to juggle the politics between the wizards, the vampires, humanity, the faeries... and also keep his sanity when someone from his past shows up and he has to rehash some old wounds.<br /><br /><i>Real fright isn't like the movies. Real fear is an ugly, quiet, relentless thing. It's a kind of pain, and I hated seeing it..."</i> pg 129, ebook<br /><br />And we can't forget Bob the Skull, one of my favorite characters. He seems to always get a few good lines in, no matter how busy the plot is.<br /><br /><i>"What's up, boss?" "Evil's afoot." "Well, sure," Bob said, "because it refuses to learn the metric system. Otherwise it'd be up to a meter by now."</i> pg 154, ebook.<br /><br />Though I had some difficulties with the way Harry behaved in the latter part of the last book, I feel like he's more of the flawed character I've come to know in this entry. Yes, he still makes mistakes sometimes and can be an idiot, but it makes more sense. There are circumstances beyond his control that are acting on his mind in ways he may not be aware of yet. But he's learning about that, and his friends won't let him get too out of hand.<br /><br />Or, at least, they'll all go down together... probably spectacularly and in flames. Highly recommended for urban fantasy readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="582792658491765645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8308719210896413023"><b>3.5/5 stars</b> <br/><br/>How much of a good thing is too much? Five books? Nine books? How about sixteen books? <b>White Night</b> was a book nine and unless something ground breaking happens I don't think I will make it to book 16 (there's more coming after that too I'm sure). <br/><br/>​This was everything that a good <b>Dresden Files</b> novel should be: witty, non-stop action with some sexual tension and hilarious remarks. But I still felt a little bit bored. Maybe because we already met the villain in the previous book. Maybe </span>
  <span id="freeText8308719210896413023" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 stars</b> <br /><br />How much of a good thing is too much? Five books? Nine books? How about sixteen books? <b>White Night</b> was a book nine and unless something ground breaking happens I don't think I will make it to book 16 (there's more coming after that too I'm sure). <br /><br />​This was everything that a good <b>Dresden Files</b> novel should be: witty, non-stop action with some sexual tension and hilarious remarks. But I still felt a little bit bored. Maybe because we already met the villain in the previous book. Maybe because the concept seemed really cool, but then everything kind of got turned around 360 degrees and I just wasn't into it? I don't know, this wasn't bad, but it wasn't particularly great either. Especially in the middle - things dragged quite a bit, despite the never ending action (I don't even know how's that possible). <br /><br />But, once again the ending was amazing and I will be definitely picking up number 10, just maybe not too soon. This is definitely not a series you can binge, it does get quite repetitive. You want to stretch them out and savor every book a good time apart from one another. Don't worry about forgetting stuff - Butcher is great about catching the reader up (one of the best really). <br /><br />​What I love most about Dresden Files, besides the hilariousness that is Harry, is how relatable and real the books are. I think the crazy attention to details largely contributes to that. I love how Butcher never forgets that Mouse is a living, breathing, pooping dog and not just a super hero side kick. I love that Harry gets cranky and tired, and he sleeps and eats like a normal functioning human. In too many books main characters are portrayed as those "super warrior machines that only keep fighting for justice, or whatever". Harry is real and I think that's the beauty of it. Also, he can make fun of himself and it's hilarious and I just love it. <br /><br />​I also especially adore Harry and Thomas's relationship - those two give me life. I really need more of their interaction in every book. Even Bob the Skull is a fantastic and well rounded character. <br /><br />​I did think that there was going to be more of Molly in this book, but I guess after being the main distorter in previous book she kind of took a step back - which is fine, I'm not particularly fond of Molly. I liked how Elaine was brought back, but also thought that there was nearly not enough of hermit all. Also, I never really liked suzan, so can we just stop mentioning her? Plus, there hasn't been a sex scene in at least two previous books, Butcher are you okay? I'm worried over here. haha. <br /><br />​Despite being a tad bored with this one I still think that these series is a great fun and I love most of these characters dearly. Especially Mouse and Thomas *heart eyes* , he got me under his vampiric charm. <br /><br />My <a href="http://bookandsword.net " rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a><br />My <a href="https://www.instagram.com/book_and_sword/" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a></span>

I think I even get a little bit overenthusiastic in some of my r</span>
  <span id="freeText10106292359390950617" style="display:none">Another pretty good Dresden book. But first thing I want to mention is the amazing narrator, James Marsters. It's the first time I listened to Dresden audiobook, and I loved it. James Marsters does an awesome job and he sounds pretty much like I imagined Harry would sound. I think I am definitely going to buy an audiobook when the next Dresden book comes out. <br /><br />If you read any of my reviews of Dresden Files, you know I am a huge fan. I think I even get a little bit overenthusiastic in some of my reviews, or give the books slightly higher rating that they actually deserve. But well, can't help myself there. These books are pretty entertaining for me, they are fast-paced and full of action, magic, supernatural creatures and awesome characters. This series is like a drug, and I am addicted. And Jim Butcher is an awesome author, and it was great to see how he improved with every next book. At the beginning, when I read Storm Front, I never though I would like this series so much. It was interesting, but nothing special. But then the series slowly started to become more complex, Jim Butcher's writing better and better, and characters deeper and more complex. Now it feels like it's really big journey and it's really cool to be part of it. And Jim Butcher's has a way to make you feel like you are part of the story. If he starts a sentence like: "Have you ever been...? Have you ever thought about...? Have you ever felt...?" It automatically makes you wonder about some things that happened to you in real life, brings back some of the memories, and then it somehow makes you feel closer to characters, or makes you understand the situation better. He is pretty good in making you feel that way, and I love that when I read his books.<br /><br />I will try not to get overenthusiastic in this review, I promise;) Of course, there are some things that I don't like about the series. First of all, since every book is told from Harry's POV, you need to like this character to enjoy the series. If you can't stand the guy, you obviously aren't going to last this long in the series. And while I really really like him, there are times that he annoys me greatly. He can be pretty whiny, he has a hero complex and he often forgets that he is not the only one who can deal with the problem or who notices things. Well, he usually is th most qualified I would say, but sometimes he is a big drama queen too. I am glad that one of the characters pointed it out to him in the end. I didn't like how he was withholding the information from one of his friends in the end. I think he should have learned that lesson by now. <br />And the other annoying thing is the fact that almost every female monster has to be pretty, sexy woman and of curse Harry can't help but notice it ever time. The amount of beautiful and sexy women in these books, who in fact are horrible monsters, makes me roll my eyes sometimes. But, we see things through Harry's eyes, and I guess he can't help it or change it. It's just who he is and how he sees some things and he is far from perfect. But I guess I wouldn't like him so much if he was perfect. And although there are some annoying things about these books, they always stay in the background, at least for me, there are just too many cool things about Dresden to make me complain about the things I don't like for too long.<br /><br />White Night is another pretty good Dresden book. It follows the usual pattern, there is a crime and Harry gets to investigate. That's how it usually starts. But it was never boring. First of all, this time I kept dreading that one of the characters I really liked was involved in the crimes. Second thing, Harry was joined by someone from his past. I don't really like her that much, but it was cool to learn more about her and it was also cool to see her in action. For once, Harry wasn't the only wizard responsible for destroying some of the buildings;)<br />Plus compared to some previous crimes, this time it was much deeper than some kind of crazy, blood-thirsty monster murdering innocent people. I love how Jim Butcher keeps revealing just a little bit of what's really going on in each book. <br />And the ending was pretty cool, it was enough to give this book 5 stars. I love magical duels. I got to see one in the end, and Harry wasn't the only wizard involved. I love reading about other wizards and see how they use magic. It's usually quite different than the way Harry uses it, and that's always pretty interesting and cool to read. And the bad guys joined the good guys to kill some of even worse bad guys in the end, and I really liked it. <br /><br />White Night might not be my favorite book of Dresden, but it's among the ones I like the most. And I liked how some of the issues were resolved in the end.<br />And I also have to mention one thing. I really appreciate the fact that Jim Butcher doesn't really kill a lot of the characters. At least so far, I am kind of dreading what happens when the final books get released, because there is no way that every character I love is going to survive. But anyway, thanks to the amount of books in this series, we really could get to know some of the characters so well, see them grow and develop. By now, they really feel like old friends. <br />This book is probably 4 or 4.5 read to be honest, but as usual with Dresden, I rounded it up to 5:)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10106292359390950617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18252746931433633350">Love this series! it's so addictive; as soon as I finish one book I want to read the next. Jim Butcher is slowly building up a massive plot, revealing only a few small teasers each book, developing the threads and strings that will all eventually be pulled together in a massive showdown.   <span id="freeText18252746931433633350" style="display:none">Love this series! it's so addictive; as soon as I finish one book I want to read the next. Jim Butcher is slowly building up a massive plot, revealing only a few small teasers each book, developing the threads and strings that will all eventually be pulled together in a massive showdown. Little hints at Harry's background are also building up slowly, working towards a big reveal. <br /><br />In this episode, Sgt Murphy calls Harry in for his unofficial opinion on a series of deaths made to look like suicides. Harry pretty soon works out that some minor magical folk are being targeted in Chicago and other cities even though the Peace Accord between the White Council of Wizards and the Vampires is still active. Other people have disappeared as well, in the company of someone who looks like Thomas, Harry's half brother. Harry soon finds himself back in the White Court of vampires, having to overthrow a deadly plot. Plenty of fast action and witty dialog make this another enjoyable read. Harry has some new gadgets to play with and we get to see more of Ramirez and in particular his wizardry in fighting skills. Molly is coming along as an apprentice and becoming less sullen teenager and more junior wizard, Harry's dog Mouse exhibits some of his hidden talents and Harry's first love, Elaine is in town adding some spice and reminders of Harry's early life. </span>

<div id="review_875497768" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/875497768" />
    <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books"><img alt="Em Lost In Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522743986p2/11166121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/875497768?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em Lost In Books" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books">Em Lost In Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2000-09">2000-09</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer875497768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer758228993942688966">Before starting the review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91475.White_Night__The_Dresden_Files___9_' title='White Night (The Dresden Files, #9) by Jim Butcher' rel='nofollow noopener'>White Night</a>, I would like to tell you how I met Harry. After devouring the Fever series by Karen Marie Moning in 2012, I wanted to read another amazing Urban Fantasy so I requested for some UF recommendations. And first time I met Harry there when I was recommended Dresden Files in response to my request. I read the blurb; saw the cover, length of the series, a male protagonist and instantly dismissed it. It was start of 2013 and had just started reading fantasy boo</span>
  <span id="freeText758228993942688966" style="display:none">Before starting the review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91475.White_Night__The_Dresden_Files___9_" title="White Night (The Dresden Files, #9) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">White Night</a>, I would like to tell you how I met Harry. After devouring the Fever series by Karen Marie Moning in 2012, I wanted to read another amazing Urban Fantasy so I requested for some UF recommendations. And first time I met Harry there when I was recommended Dresden Files in response to my request. I read the blurb; saw the cover, length of the series, a male protagonist and instantly dismissed it. It was start of 2013 and had just started reading fantasy books at that time, so I searched Google for most awaited fantasy books of 2012. I opened the very first link and checked the list. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12216302.Cold_Days__The_Dresden_Files___14_" title="Cold Days (The Dresden Files, #14) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Cold Days</a> was sitting prettily at number four with this description:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“For those who have never heard of Harry Dresden, where have you been!? Harry Dresden is a private investigator who also has the added advantages (and disadvantages at times) of being a wizard. They are written in the sarcastic first person voice of Harry who tends to get hired in order to uncover the facts behind some kind of supernatural murder or crime.<br /><br />The first couple of books were okay, nothing really breathtakingly brilliant about them, but from there they picked up and have quickly become fan favorites. Each novel is relatively short, but they certainly back a lot of great content in-between those covers.”</i>
</b><br /><br />&amp; I finally decided to read Dresden Files but still it took me almost seven months to start this. I didn’t liked it much and my friend who’d recommended it to me in first place told me to have some patience. So I kept reading Mr Dresden’s story, and after finishing ninth book (&amp; I’m almost 80% done with tenth right now) I’m glad I did not abandoned it after reading first book. <br /><br />One of the best thing about this series is that the quality of books gets better with every new addition to the series and that says a lot as book #15 is coming out this June (&amp; according to Wikipedia Mr Butcher is going to add another five books to this series and there will be a trilogy too after that). Mr Butcher’s writing skill has improved a lot since the first book. Maintaining this level of quality with one book per year on average is amazing. Now he don’t go in details to tell about a person from previous books. Readers have to rake their own brains for recognition. <br /><br />So now back to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91475.White_Night__The_Dresden_Files___9_" title="White Night (The Dresden Files, #9) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">White Night</a>, this book starts with Harry being called by Murphy to a murder scene. Murder looked like a plain suicide, but a clue left at the crime scene told Harry that the victim was a magic practitioner. Murphy told Harry that there were more murders like this. One clue led to the other and they all points to Thomas Raith (a person very dear to Harry) and made him a prime suspect. Now it was up to Harry to clear Thomas’s name. <br /><br />White Night is a fast paced story that keeps you to the edge till you finish it. You don’t know what is going to happen on the next page. Mr Butcher has blended mystery and action so well here. The climax action scene is my second favorite in this series (of course first place go to the dinosaur scene from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17683.Dead_Beat__The_Dresden_Files__7_" title="Dead Beat (The Dresden Files #7) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Beat</a>). <br /><br />This is a highly entertaining and excellent read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="758228993942688966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-before-goodreads">read-before-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=dresden-files">dresden-files</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362649775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer506589386046750019"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This is one of three books from the Dresden Files series I've given 5 stars to, and if you follow my reviews, you know that's something I try not to do lightly. I really enjoy it start to finish.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> I could just copy paste this section from book to book. James Marsters is great. If you've been reading my previous reviews or listening to this series yourself you know that. Highlights in this book include him actually yelling during one scene and this crazy french accent</span>
  <span id="freeText506589386046750019" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This is one of three books from the Dresden Files series I've given 5 stars to, and if you follow my reviews, you know that's something I try not to do lightly. I really enjoy it start to finish.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> I could just copy paste this section from book to book. James Marsters is great. If you've been reading my previous reviews or listening to this series yourself you know that. Highlights in this book include him actually yelling during one scene and this crazy french accent.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />So I finally arrived to what was for years my favorite Dresden book. I'm still not quite sure, but I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6585201.Changes__The_Dresden_Files___12_" title="Changes (The Dresden Files, #12) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Changes</a> edges this out for best in the series.<br /><br />This is the book that turned me into a herald for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10746.Jim_Butcher" title="Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Jim Butcher</a>. I couldn't shut up about this series for awhile. I would tell anyone who would listen they should read this series. (NOTE: This happened a second time after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12216302.Cold_Days__The_Dresden_Files___14_" title="Cold Days (The Dresden Files, #14) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Cold Days</a> last year.)<br /><br />Now this isn't a life changing book or something. It just one of those books I have trouble putting down. Page-turning fun. In fact I spent at least 2 hours doing nothing else but listening to the ending. Normally I'm driving, riding my bike, running errands or doing stuff around the house. I ran out of stuff to do to keep listening, so I just sat in my easy chair and finished it.<br /><br />Gone is the stranger coming to Harry's office. Gone is the introduction to some new characters/aspects of Harry's world. Mr. Butcher simply takes all the building blocks he established in the previous books to tell a really fun story, with a truly awesome ending.<br /><br />I'm probably overselling this book. Only one of my friends I've since recommended this to seems to love this book as much as I do, and he stubbornly refuses to admit <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6585201.Changes__The_Dresden_Files___12_" title="Changes (The Dresden Files, #12) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Changes</a> is a better book. Still, if you don't thoroughly enjoy this book, why are you still reading this series?<br /><br />Murphy calls Dresden to check out a crime scene off the books. A woman is dead. It turns out a lot of them are. They appear to have committed suicide, but something just seems off.<br /><br />If you know this series, you know if there is one thing that turns Harry Dresden from well reason detective to charge in first ask questions later neanderthal, it's when someone is hurting women. Especially in his town.<br /><br />Harry is going to do whatever it takes to put a stop to it, even if it kills him. <br /><br />We finally get to see Harry be a true badass in this book. There have been glimmers before, but nothing quite like this. With my vague memory of the next few books, it's something we won't quite see again until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6585201.Changes__The_Dresden_Files___12_" title="Changes (The Dresden Files, #12) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Changes</a> either.<br /><br />This book shows that both Harry Dresden and Jim Butcher have both matured into something more then when they started.</span>
  <a data-text-id="506589386046750019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures"><img alt="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463631966p2/7742509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2565039452?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)" href="/user/show/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures">Angela (Angel&#39;s Guilty Pleasures)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=fav-urban-fantasy">fav-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=fav-magic-books">fav-magic-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7742509-angela-angel-s-guilty-pleasures?shelf=library-love">library-love</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2565039452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4695895396273306319"><b>White Night</b> opens around a year after the previous book. Harry and his apprentice Molly are investigating a rash of suspicious murders. Someone of something is killing off those practitioners who barely have any power/magic. <br/><br/>I always feel a little lost when I first start theses books. It has to do with the time in-between when one book ends to when the next one starts. I’m reading one a month, but each book has like a year difference in them and so, I feel like I’m miss something like maybe a no</span>
  <span id="freeText4695895396273306319" style="display:none"><b>White Night</b> opens around a year after the previous book. Harry and his apprentice Molly are investigating a rash of suspicious murders. Someone of something is killing off those practitioners who barely have any power/magic. <br><br>I always feel a little lost when I first start theses books. It has to do with the time in-between when one book ends to when the next one starts. I’m reading one a month, but each book has like a year difference in them and so, I feel like I’m miss something like maybe a novella or short story that I needed to read, but once I get into the book I’m all in until the bitter end.<br><br>I really enjoy these books. Harry, I like the balance of dark and light within him. It feels real. We all have light and dark in ourselves and each day is a battle to keep them balanced. I also really enjoy the secondary characters; like Murphy, Thomas, Johnny Marcone, Ramirez, and others. They bring with them some fun, interesting, and enjoyable moments. <br><br>I was pleasantly happy to see Johnny Marcone, Chicago’s notorious underworld boss return. He’s a dark character, but he’s also a good man. We finally learn who the mystery girl is that Johnny is hiding away and taking care of. Murphy and Thomas where amazingly awesome in this installment. Murphy is one of my favorite characters and I wish Harry and Murphy would get together, but they are just friends, but I keep hoping. Thomas has some secrets in this installment and one that was a fun moment to read when Harry found out. Molly, well she got on my nerves with her complete disregard for her actions and how they impact others. I get she’s young and learning, but still. The only character I didn’t like seeing was Harry’s teenage girlfriend who comes back. I don’t know. It probably has to do with me wanting Harry and Murphy together. <br><br><i>The Dresden Files</i> are always packed full of action, mystery, and suspense. The different storylines all work well together and seeing Harry constantly struggle with morals, a fallen angel, and more intrigues me. <br><br><b>
  <i>White Night</i>
</b> had a lot to offer and I can’t wait to discover what nonsense Harry finds himself in next. <br><br><b>Rated: 4 Stars</b><br><br><a href="http://angelsguiltypleasures.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466193893i/19451911.jpg" width="400" height="100" alt="angelsgp-seethisreview-blure" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_2158322044" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2158322044" />
    <a title="Tosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43670791-tosh"><img alt="Tosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515175943p2/43670791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2158322044?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tosh" href="/user/show/43670791-tosh">Tosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43670791-tosh?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43670791-tosh?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43670791-tosh?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43670791-tosh?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2158322044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12755103432626466635"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Evil’s afoot.<br/><br/>Well, sure...because it refuses to learn the metric system. Otherwise it’d be up to a meter by now.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I’m not usually one to push so quickly through a series, but I’m thoroughly enjoying myself and can’t seem to pull myself away. <br/><br/>With every installment Harry is becoming stronger and more experienced, while implementing interesting tools and forming unlikely alliances to aid him. Meaning, the action only gets better. <i>Next to Sue</i> the magical mayhem and fight sequences in this</span>
  <span id="freeText12755103432626466635" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Evil’s afoot.<br /><br />Well, sure...because it refuses to learn the metric system. Otherwise it’d be up to a meter by now.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I’m not usually one to push so quickly through a series, but I’m thoroughly enjoying myself and can’t seem to pull myself away. <br /><br />With every installment Harry is becoming stronger and more experienced, while implementing interesting tools and forming unlikely alliances to aid him. Meaning, the action only gets better. <i>Next to Sue</i> the magical mayhem and fight sequences in this book were some of the best so far. The tension was so thick in the last few chapters, Mr. Butcher actually had me worried something terrible was going to befall one of my beloved characters. And no doubt this far into the series someone’s luck is bound run out. The stakes are getting higher. The more Harry pushes back and interferes the worse it seems to get, the greater the threats seem to be, and the more power he and his peers have to expend to stop them. Makes for some pretty intense scenes and increasingly clever means to outmatch each new obstacle. <br /><br />But the action isn’t the only thing holding my attention. Outside the supernatural craziness and feats of wizardry there’s some everyday drama and fabulous side characters. It’s hard not to get caught up in the details, or the directness with which Harry handles his relationships, everyday issues, and his ongoing internal ones. Not to mention the heavy dose of humor he liberally spreads on every situation - sometimes unintentionally. There are tons of laugh out loud moments, and equally profound ones as well. It’s always good fun when the MC can share a bit of wisdom in one sentence and turn around to hit you with some humor the next. I love a smartass :)<br /><br />So yes, another great installment in the series and I can’t wait to continue. <br /><br /><i>No one likes a wiseass, Harry.<br /><br />Are you kidding? As long as the wiseass is talking to someone else, people love 'em.</i><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12755103432626466635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/686345817?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/12414384-white-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer686345817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3624757083102588738">Another action packed episode. Murphy asks Dresden to unofficially look into a series of staged suicides. Things go pear shaped from there.<br/><br/>This felt a little “episodic” to me in that there’s not a lot we haven’t seen before. Ghouls and Vampires. Lots of them. There’s plenty of action though and Harry has beefed up a lot of his magical <i>accessories</i> for that bit of extra punch – a regional commander of the Wardens of the White Council needs a bit of extra juice after all – especially in the middle </span>
  <span id="freeText3624757083102588738" style="display:none">Another action packed episode. Murphy asks Dresden to unofficially look into a series of staged suicides. Things go pear shaped from there.<br /><br />This felt a little “episodic” to me in that there’s not a lot we haven’t seen before. Ghouls and Vampires. Lots of them. There’s plenty of action though and Harry has beefed up a lot of his magical <i>accessories</i> for that bit of extra punch – a regional commander of the Wardens of the White Council needs a bit of extra juice after all – especially in the middle of a war with the Red Court Vampires.<br /><br />The action at the end of the book was pretty intense. Lots of guns, lots of Hell Fire, lots of blood and lots of ichor - Harry really cuts loose. James Marsters also really cuts loose with his Harry Dresden “belly yell” – nothing a change of pants can’t overcome. <br /><br />Molly Carpenter features, playing her part as Harry’s Apprentice and we have some familiar bad guys return- one in particular who was supposed to be dead.<br /><br />Oh...and Harry comes out of the closet. So does Thomas. Oops.<br /><br />I don’t know about the other Wardens, but Harry wears the “grey” cloak well – ‘cause a lot of his actions, and some of the alliances he makes involve cosying up to some pretty nasty characters – not everything is black and white – sometimes it’s a case of living with the “devil you know” – particularly the ones on the inside.<br /><br />3.5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3624757083102588738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1308360215" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1308360215" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1308360215?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841496870" href="/book/show/927975.White_Night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1308360215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1879540803026150982">8/10<br/> <br/>These are getting harder to review as the series goes on. 9 books in now and I feel confident that the reviews I write will be pretty standard throughout the series. The majority will be 4 stars as the quality of writing is good, the characters well rounded with enough development throughout the series to keep it from being stale, the plot getting more complicated with each passing novel but still easily digestible. There will be some that fail to meet that 4 star mark and some which shoot </span>
  <span id="freeText1879540803026150982" style="display:none">8/10<br /> <br />These are getting harder to review as the series goes on. 9 books in now and I feel confident that the reviews I write will be pretty standard throughout the series. The majority will be 4 stars as the quality of writing is good, the characters well rounded with enough development throughout the series to keep it from being stale, the plot getting more complicated with each passing novel but still easily digestible. There will be some that fail to meet that 4 star mark and some which shoot over it (only with the aid of Polka though).<br /><br />This one is no different. The plot is more complicated than say the earlier novels, and rely on your knowledge of previous novels to get you on board with what is going on and who all the major players are. There are handy little reminders throughout but done in a way which jogs the memory rather than gives bullet point summary of what has gone before which is a nice touch but may get tedious if reading back to back.<br /><br />There are a few scenes in this one which stood out, none more so than the climatic ending. This was quite the finale and was tense in parts with a great mix of action, plot reveals and backs to wall scenarios but always knowing things would work out (the continuation of the series is a giveaway there!). For some reason the climatic ending reminded me of playing Gears of War. No idea why, but I’m going to pick that game up again now!<br /><br />All in all, if you’ve read this far in the series then you’re likely to continue and you won’t be disappointed. This is another wise solid read in the series. If you’ve not started the series then I recommend giving it a whirl (at least up until book 4 to get a real feel for the series). I’d probably struggle somewhat with the series were I to read them back to back as they may become a little samey however reading them with a couple of months break in between is working out well for me. I look forward to picking the next one up in the near future. <br /><br />If you enjoyed this try: “Gears of War” by Xbox</span>
  <a data-text-id="1879540803026150982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1163145349?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1163145349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15343634854801903">Harry Dresden is back and just like every previous book in this series, its better than it's predecessors. <br/><br/>I take my hat off to you Jim Butcher. It feels like we as readers have taken this journey with you as you started out in this career and you really have gone from strength to strength. This is also very evident in the evolution of the characters on your pages. They have become such complex and well liked beings that I doubt the author could off any one of them without a huge backlash from h</span>
  <span id="freeText15343634854801903" style="display:none">Harry Dresden is back and just like every previous book in this series, its better than it's predecessors. <br /><br />I take my hat off to you Jim Butcher. It feels like we as readers have taken this journey with you as you started out in this career and you really have gone from strength to strength. This is also very evident in the evolution of the characters on your pages. They have become such complex and well liked beings that I doubt the author could off any one of them without a huge backlash from his fans. <br /><br />As always, the dialogue is top notch and the banter just makes for a so much more enjoyable read. The plot was fairly tight, twisty and felt much more layered than his earlier books, yet easily followable. I do admit that while I thought this book was pretty amazing, I never fell into that cannot-put-it-down mode that you get from your most favourite reads. I considered giving this a firm 4, but I cannot find anything negative to say about White Night, so I'm giving it the benefit of a full house of stars. <br /><br />Highly recommended.<br /><br /></span>
